<P STYLE="margin: 0; text-align: right"><B>Exhibit 99.1</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin: 0">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-left: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="text-align: center; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Reliance Steel &amp; Aluminum Co. Reports Second Quarter
2015 Financial Results</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">- EPS of $1.20<BR>
<BR>
- Cash flow from operations of $292.5 million</P>

<P STYLE="margin-left: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin: 0pt 0">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">LOS ANGELES, July 23, 2015 /PRNewswire/ -- Reliance Steel &amp; Aluminum Co. (NYSE:
RS) today reported its financial results for the second quarter ended June 30, 2015.</P>

<P STYLE="text-align: left; font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; color: Red; margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><IMG SRC="logo.jpg" ALT=""></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Second Quarter 2015 Financial Highlights</B></P>

<UL STYLE="list-style-type: disc">

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Sales were $2.42 billion, down 7.4% from $2.62 billion in the second quarter of
2014 and down 7.3% from $2.61 billion in the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Tons sold were down 2.1% from the second quarter of 2014 and down 2.4% from the
first quarter of 2015, with the average selling price per ton sold down 6.0% from the second quarter of 2014 and down 5.2% from
the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Net income attributable to Reliance was $90.2 million, down 6.5% from $96.5 million
in the second quarter of 2014 and down 11.0% from $101.3 million in the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Earnings per diluted share were $1.20, down 1.6% from $1.22 in the second quarter
of 2014 and down 7.7% from $1.30 in the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Non-GAAP earnings per diluted share were $1.21, down 6.9% from $1.30 in both the
second quarter of 2014 and the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">A pre-tax LIFO credit, or income, of $32.5 million, is included in cost of sales
compared to a pre-tax LIFO charge, or expense, of $5.0 million in the second quarter of 2014 and a credit of $7.5 million in the
first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">The effective tax rate was 32.6%, compared to 36.6% in the second quarter of 2014
and 31.7% in the first quarter of 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Cash flow from operations was $292.5 million, up from $40.7 million in the second
quarter of 2014, and net debt-to-total capital was 33.9% at June 30, 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Reliance repurchased $200.0 million of its common stock, or 4.4% of December 31,
2014 shares outstanding, in the first half of 2015.&#160; The Company repurchased an additional $61.5 million of shares in July
2015, to-date.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">A quarterly cash dividend of $0.40 per share was declared on July 21, 2015 for
shareholders of record as of August 14, 2015 and will be payable on September 11, 2015.</LI>

</UL>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Management Commentary</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&#34;I am extremely pleased with our operational performance in the second quarter
of 2015, which is a testament to the quality of our management in the field as well as to our business model,&#34; said Gregg Mollins,
President and Chief Executive Officer of Reliance. &#34;Despite ongoing industry headwinds that further pressured metals pricing
in the 2015 second quarter, we were able to increase our FIFO gross profit margin to 25.7%, up from our strong 2015 first quarter
level of 25.4%. We believe our long-standing practice of focusing on small, quick turnaround orders, our focus on inventory turnover
and our increased investments which provide higher levels of value-added processing to our customers, has allowed us to experience
this margin consistency in a difficult business environment. We believe that customer demand is relatively strong and will continue
to slowly improve, even though our second quarter demand levels were somewhat lower than we had anticipated. Currently, we see
ongoing strength and opportunities for growth in the aerospace end-market and through our toll processing operations related to
the automotive market. Although still below peak demand levels, we also continue to be encouraged by momentum in our non-residential
construction businesses.&#34;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Mr. Mollins continued, &#34;Pricing for all commodity types remained weak primarily
due to the historically high levels of imports in the marketplace, resulting in a 5.2% decline in our average selling price per
ton sold compared to the prior quarter. Although price changes impact our earnings levels, we believe our disciplined focus on
managing all controllable aspects of the business continues to mitigate the negative impact from the difficult market conditions
we are currently experiencing. We reduced our FIFO inventory by $163.0 million during the second quarter of 2015, a key area of
focus for Reliance. Using our tons on hand at June 30, 2015, our inventory turnover rate was 4.6 times based on first half 2015
shipment volumes, compared to 4.3 times in the prior quarter, approaching our goal of 4.75 turns. This contributed to significant
cash flow generation that we were able to use for growth initiatives, shareholder returns and debt reduction.&#34;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>End-market Commentary</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">During the second quarter of 2015, Reliance experienced relatively steady customer
demand across most of its end-markets, with the exception of the energy market which continued to decline. Although the demand
momentum experienced in the 2015 first quarter lessened, the Company expects that underlying demand will improve from current levels
during the second half of the year, subject to normal seasonal factors.</P>

<UL STYLE="list-style-type: disc">

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Automotive demand, supported mainly by the Company&#39;s toll processing operations
in the U.S. and Mexico, was very strong and is expected to continue at current production rates throughout the remainder of 2015.&#160;
The increase in aluminum usage in the automotive industry continues to represent a growth area for Reliance.&#160;&#160;</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Aerospace demand continued to improve during the second quarter and is expected
to continue to grow as 2015 progresses and as &#34;build&#34; rates increase.&#160;</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Heavy industry continues to perform reasonably well.&#160; Although agricultural
and construction equipment demand has declined, Reliance remains active in these markets.&#160;</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Non-residential construction continues to improve, but remains well below peak
levels. Reliance believes that this important end-market will maintain positive growth throughout 2015.</LI>

<LI STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Energy (oil and gas) demand for the products Reliance sells has declined significantly
due to the severe drop in oil prices and is expected to remain under pressure throughout the remainder of 2015.&#160; Reliance&#39;s
shipment volumes for its energy businesses were down 34% in the first half of 2015 compared to the first half of 2014.</LI>

</UL>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Balance Sheet &amp; Liquidity</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">The Company generated $292.5 million in cash flow from operating activities in the
second quarter of 2015 and $463.9 million in the first six months of 2015. In the second quarter of 2015, the Company paid down
$156.0 million of debt. As of June 30, 2015, total debt outstanding was $2.20 billion, for a net debt-to-total capital ratio of
33.9%, compared to 36.2% at March 31, 2015. The Company had $585.0 million in outstanding borrowings on its $1.5 billion revolving
credit facility at June 30, 2015.</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&#34;We were pleased with our strong liquidity position at quarter end, which highlights
our ability to effectively manage our working capital and consistently generate significant cash flow throughout difficult industry
cycles,&#34; said Karla Lewis, Senior Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer of Reliance. &#34;Our healthy liquidity
position affords us the flexibility and resources to continue investing in the growth of our business, both organically and through
M&amp;A opportunities. At the same time we continue to provide enhanced returns to our shareholders through our quarterly dividends
and by using excess cash to opportunistically repurchase shares of our common stock. Furthermore, we remain focused on de-leveraging
our balance sheet, as we did during the second quarter by using our strong cash flow to significantly reduce our debt levels.&#34;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Corporate Developments</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">On July 21, 2015, the Board of Directors declared a quarterly cash dividend of $0.40
per share of common stock, payable on September 11, 2015 to shareholders of record as of August 14, 2015. The Company has paid
regular quarterly dividends for 56 consecutive years and has increased the dividend 22 times since the 1994 IPO.</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">During the three months ended June 30, 2015, the Company repurchased $15.1 million
of its common stock under its existing share repurchase plan. Reliance&#39;s total repurchases in the first half of 2015 were 3.4
million shares at an average cost of $58.17 per share for a total of $200.0 million. At June 30, 2015, approximately 3.7 million
shares remained available for repurchase under the share repurchase plan. The Company has repurchased an additional $61.5 million
of its shares in July 2015, to-date, and expects to continue to opportunistically repurchase shares of its common stock going forward.</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>Business Outlook </B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Reliance management expects the U.S. economy will resume its modest improvement
throughout the remainder of 2015. With the exception of the Company&#39;s businesses directly servicing the energy markets, management
expects underlying demand to generally strengthen from second quarter levels, subject to normal seasonal patterns. That said, Reliance
expects a decrease in tons sold of approximately 1% to 2% in the third quarter of 2015 over the second quarter of 2015, compared
to the more typical seasonal trend of down 3% to 5%. Although metals pricing is expected to remain under pressure for most products
the Company sells, management expects a slight improvement in overall pricing in the third quarter of 2015 over the second quarter
of 2015 with overall average selling price expected to be flat to up 1%. As a result, management currently expects earnings per
diluted share to be in the range of $0.95 to $1.05 for the third quarter ending September 30, 2015.</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt"><B>About Reliance Steel &amp; Aluminum Co.</B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">Reliance Steel &amp; Aluminum Co., headquartered in Los Angeles, California, is
the largest metals service center company in North America. Through a network of more than 300 locations in 39 states and 12 countries
outside of the United States, Reliance provides value-added metals processing services and distributes a full line of over 100,000
metal products to more than 125,000 customers in a broad range of industries.</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top: 0pt; margin-bottom: 0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TR STYLE="vertical-align: bottom">
    <TD STYLE="padding-right: 0; padding-left: 0; padding-top: 0; text-indent: 0">
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0">1 Gross profit, calculated as net sales less cost of sales,
        and gross profit margin, calculated as gross profit divided by net sales, are non-GAAP financial measures as they exclude depreciation
        and amortization expense associated with the corresponding sales. The majority of our orders are basic distribution with no processing
        services performed.&nbsp; For the remainder of our sales orders, we perform &quot;first-stage&quot; processing which is generally
        not labor intensive as we are simply cutting the metal to size.&nbsp; Because of this, the amount of related labor and overhead,
        including depreciation and amortization, are not significant and are excluded from our cost of sales. Therefore, our cost of sales
        is primarily comprised of the cost of the material we sell.&nbsp; We use gross profit and gross profit margin as shown above as
        measures of operating performance.&nbsp; Gross profit and gross profit margin are important operating and financial measures, as
        their fluctuations can have a significant impact on our earnings. &nbsp;Gross profit and gross profit margin, as presented, are
        not necessarily comparable with similarly titled measures for other companies.</P>
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-indent: 0.5in">&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR STYLE="vertical-align: bottom">
    <TD STYLE="padding-right: 0; padding-left: 0; padding-top: 0; text-indent: 0">
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0">2 See accompanying Non-GAAP earnings reconciliation.</P>
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-indent: 0.5in">&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR STYLE="vertical-align: bottom">
    <TD STYLE="padding-right: 0; padding-left: 0; padding-top: 0; text-indent: 0">
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0">3 Net debt-to-total capital is calculated as total debt (net
        of cash) divided by total Reliance stockholders' equity plus total debt (net of cash). The December 31, 2014 percentage has been
        retrospectively adjusted pursuant to our adoption of accounting changes related to the presentation of debt issuance costs.</P>
        <P STYLE="font: 10pt Times New Roman, Times, Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-indent: 0.5in">&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
<TR STYLE="vertical-align: bottom">

        attributable to Reliance and beginning total Reliance stockholders' equity.</P>
